        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11428790-the-tenderness-of-wolves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=north-america">north-america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=2018-top-25">2018-top-25</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=extreme-cold">extreme-cold</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=journeys">journeys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50297885-joy-d?shelf=zck">zck</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542736339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2467986431956251118">In this historical fiction set in the Canadian wilderness in the mid-19th century, a French-Canadian trapper living near an isolated village is found murdered in his bed. Our protagonist, Mrs. Ross, discovers the body and alerts the authorities. Upon returning home she finds that her seventeen-year-old son, Francis, a friend of the murdered man, has disappeared. Suspicion falls upon her son and a mixed-race tracker. After her husband searches, but fails to find Francis, she and the tracker set o</span>
  <span id="freeText2467986431956251118" style="display:none">In this historical fiction set in the Canadian wilderness in the mid-19th century, a French-Canadian trapper living near an isolated village is found murdered in his bed. Our protagonist, Mrs. Ross, discovers the body and alerts the authorities. Upon returning home she finds that her seventeen-year-old son, Francis, a friend of the murdered man, has disappeared. Suspicion falls upon her son and a mixed-race tracker. After her husband searches, but fails to find Francis, she and the tracker set off to locate him and determine what happened. This book contains an intricately woven mystery, with several subordinate mysteries embedded into the main storyline. The Canadian legacy of fur-trapping and the Hudson Bay Company play an important role in the narrative.<br /><br />This book is filled with striking characters, such as the ambitious and ruthless company-man in charge of the investigation, his inexperienced assistant whose heart is in the right place but makes questionable decisions, two daughters of the town magistrate that engender romantic feelings in the assistant, and a Native American guide serving as a personal protector. The author offers insight into human motivations, complexities and incongruities of character, and the yearning for answers, sometimes at the cost of inventing a solution. <br /><br />It is divided into four sections with many short chapters using different narrative perspectives. The setting becomes a significant part of the story. The writing style is eloquent. The atmospheric descriptions of the harsh landscape of the Canadian winter deliver an almost palpable feeling of icy desolation. Like the titular wolf, people can be misunderstood or judged by their appearance. The author deftly explores this theme in subtle ways throughout the story, showing we are often wrong about that which we do not understand. <br /><br />An amazing amalgamation of history, adventure, betrayal, tragic loss, and forbidden love, it is not solely a riveting mystery but also an impressive literary achievement. Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2467986431956251118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14693396770862387631">I appreciated the imagination it took for a British writer to convey the hardscrabble existence of life in remote northern Ontario in the late 1860�s without ever having been there. The murder of a trapper and disappearance of Mrs. Ross� teenage son sets her, friends of the trapper, town officials, and representative of Hudson�s Bay Company on various paths to resolve the mystery, leading different parties to carry out dangerous treks to distant settlements in the middle of winter. We get a nice</span>
  <span id="freeText14693396770862387631" style="display:none">I appreciated the imagination it took for a British writer to convey the hardscrabble existence of life in remote northern Ontario in the late 1860�s without ever having been there. The murder of a trapper and disappearance of Mrs. Ross� teenage son sets her, friends of the trapper, town officials, and representative of Hudson�s Bay Company on various paths to resolve the mystery, leading different parties to carry out dangerous treks to distant settlements in the middle of winter. We get a nice balance between the beauty versus the dangers of the wilderness and between independent human resilience and need to find trust and love with others. It�s a little odd to alternate between the narrative for Mrs. Ross in first person and that for other key characters in third person. The Ojibwe (Chippewa) characters appear to me as rendered either as overly romanticized or mysterious. Still it�s a satisfying quest of a mother taking risks to save her son and portrayal of the range of human motivations that drive people to good and evil in the context of a remote environment. The captivating title is a bit mystifying. I suppose that Mrs. Ross comes to feel awe and respect for wolves in her journeys somehow stands for feeling more apart of wild nature than opposed to it, which is reflected also in her growing affection and trust for the part Indian tracker who accompanies her.</span>

<div id="review_19327014" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/19327014" />
    <a title="Shana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/716578-shana"><img alt="Shana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199404460p2/716578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/19327014?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shana" href="/user/show/716578-shana">Shana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416571308" href="/book/show/2071731.The_Tenderness_of_Wolves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer19327014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3520932174423522187">I picked this up at Penn Station one evening when I was unexpectedly stuck in NYC. I couldn't decide which book to buy, and my boyfriend made the decision for me. (I think he picked it because his last name means wolves.)<br/><br/>I started to read, and I was immediately struck by the interesting choice of having only one character in first person. The other chapters, though not in first person, are for the most part closely aligned with a single character. I could see why Penney chose Mrs. Ross for her f</span>
  <span id="freeText3520932174423522187" style="display:none">I picked this up at Penn Station one evening when I was unexpectedly stuck in NYC. I couldn't decide which book to buy, and my boyfriend made the decision for me. (I think he picked it because his last name means wolves.)<br /><br />I started to read, and I was immediately struck by the interesting choice of having only one character in first person. The other chapters, though not in first person, are for the most part closely aligned with a single character. I could see why Penney chose Mrs. Ross for her first person voice. I found her interesting and very easy to like and sympathize with.<br /><br />That said, I never fell for this book, but even then, it is more complicated. I've read a few other reviews, and one said that though the reader never connected with the novel, she kept picking it up. A similar thing happened to me. In so many ways, I felt like the novel fell short. Like some other readers, I was quite surprised that the novel was a Costa award-winner. I just didn't feel it was award-winning good. However, I kept coming back to it. I mostly read it on the train to and from work, and I would be disappointed when I arrived.<br /><br />In the end, though, I was just disappointed. The characters and story were interesting, as were some of the creative choices like the episodic structure and the choice to have one first person voice mixed in with the third person voices. Unfortunately, the writing was not on the same level as the the other elements, and in fact, the quality of the writing was a bit erratic. Some parts were far superior to others. Furthermore, as the novel went on and each chapter had its own mini-cliffhangers, I got a little annoyed. It felt like I was watching a TV show (Another reviewer mentioned a soap opera.) instead of reading a book, and the cliffhangers weren't all that exciting, either. Most elements of the mystery were way too transparent. Another big problem for me was the loose ends Penney left. I have no problem with loose ends on principle, but I just felt like she was leaving something open for a sequel. I don't want to feel that way about a book.<br /><br />Even with my reservations and my disappointments, I don't think that reading this book was a waste of time. I'm confident that most readers will not be sorry.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3520932174423522187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_90875429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90875429" />
    <a title="Tara Chevrestt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2544368-tara-chevrestt"><img alt="Tara Chevrestt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399003936p2/2544368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90875429?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Chevrestt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Chevrestt" href="/user/show/2544368-tara-chevrestt">Tara Chevrestt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=canada">canada</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90875429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2017512823077446071">First of all, let me make it clear.. I read the whole thing and I am still scratching my head in confusion. What begins as a mystery in a trapper's cabin in 1867 ends with me wrinkling my nose in distaste in 2010. <br/><br/>Laurent Jammett is found dead in his cabin. His throat is slashed. A few things are missing. Whodunit and why? It takes 300 some pages and around 25 characters with their entire life stories, thoughts, and desires to answer that question. And the answer left me rather disappointed. I s</span>
  <span id="freeText2017512823077446071" style="display:none">First of all, let me make it clear.. I read the whole thing and I am still scratching my head in confusion. What begins as a mystery in a trapper's cabin in 1867 ends with me wrinkling my nose in distaste in 2010. <br /><br />Laurent Jammett is found dead in his cabin. His throat is slashed. A few things are missing. Whodunit and why? It takes 300 some pages and around 25 characters with their entire life stories, thoughts, and desires to answer that question. And the answer left me rather disappointed. I sat there and I said, "All this reading.. two days of my life.. and he died for this?" <br /><br />I failed to see what a lot of things had to do with the main story, or even the secondary story. Mrs. Ross's memories of the mental asylum, Francis and Susannah's brief "relationship", Line's sexual desires and whatever, the homosexuality angle, I expected all this to tie in somehow in the end, but a lot of it was irrelevant to the story line. These things had nothing to do with the murder. I did enjoy the parts about the long lost missing girls, but found myself disappointed that there are really no wolves in the telling of this tale. I don't really count the brief part in which it is suspected that a wolf ate a horse. <br /><br />And darn it, you would think they would have at least told us the heorine's first name. What is up with that last page? Two stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2017512823077446071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_191139367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191139367" />
    <a title="Shoma Patnaik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4988520-shoma-patnaik"><img alt="Shoma Patnaik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485227285p2/4988520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191139367?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shoma Patnaik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shoma Patnaik" href="/user/show/4988520-shoma-patnaik">Shoma Patnaik</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4988520-shoma-patnaik?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4988520-shoma-patnaik?shelf=rural">rural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4988520-shoma-patnaik?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4988520-shoma-patnaik?shelf=canada">canada</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191139367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12733636192217518598">It was the setting that drew me to this novel, but no matter how beautiful Stef Penney's depiction of the frozen wilderness of 19th century Canada, it couldn't salvage the book.<br/><br/>From the beginning, this book read like the middling novelization of a possibly interesting movie. I found out later that the author is a scriptwriter so that might have something to do with it. The problem is basically indifferent writing and incomplete characters. The protagonist, Mrs. Ross could have been interesting b</span>
  <span id="freeText12733636192217518598" style="display:none">It was the setting that drew me to this novel, but no matter how beautiful Stef Penney's depiction of the frozen wilderness of 19th century Canada, it couldn't salvage the book.<br /><br />From the beginning, this book read like the middling novelization of a possibly interesting movie. I found out later that the author is a scriptwriter so that might have something to do with it. The problem is basically indifferent writing and incomplete characters. The protagonist, Mrs. Ross could have been interesting but I just couldn't see her at all. Her narrations in first-person couldn't merge very well with the rest of the book, in third person. There were far too many storylines fighting to be heard within the book and since they had more or less bland characters, you can't really get involved with any of them. The subplot with Line and the one with Francis and Jammet could have been done away with, or at least written better. Randomly inserting token homosexual characters is very tiresome. Is it so difficult to create a character who's both gay and well-thought out? Unfortunately Penney isn't alone in this. <br /><br />The Native American characters are equally uni-dimensional; you're just repeatedly told of the "half-breeds" and how alien and savage they are without attempting to give them real personalities. Kahon'wes had promise but he barely saunters into the story, and as little other than an alcoholic. Alcoholism was and is a serious concern in Indian communities, but Penney handles it clumsily - in her story alcohol seems to only induce Indians into making an Olympic sport out of knifing white settlers. Perhaps the author had good intentions but they just don't translate well into writing. I don't know if the author wanted to make Parker "mysterious" but the attempt has instead resulted in a potentially interesting character becoming yet another bland element in the story. Who is Parker? What moves him? What does he fear and what does he like? You get nothing. The ending was just plain lazy, as if the author couldn't wait to be done with the book and just added something vaguely philosophical to wrap it up. <br /><br />All in all, this would have been a better movie than a book. At least the nature scenes would be good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12733636192217518598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2009777503" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2009777503" />
    <a title="Stef Rozitis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31302654-stef-rozitis"><img alt="Stef Rozitis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528589606p2/31302654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009777503?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stef Rozitis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stef Rozitis" href="/user/show/31302654-stef-rozitis">Stef Rozitis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302654-stef-rozitis?shelf=2001-2010">2001-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302654-stef-rozitis?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302654-stef-rozitis?shelf=read-women-2017">read-women-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302654-stef-rozitis?shelf=read-around-the-world">read-around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302654-stef-rozitis?shelf=set-canada">set-canada</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009777503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16644415238793038775">This was a very interesting book, sensitively written and complex and managed to have elements of romance in it without putting me off too much (anyone who follows my reviews will be surprised by this). It's a tad on the bleak and tragic side, although at least it constantly humanises and rehumanises characters.<br/><br/>Two of my gripes were the overall negativity of it (everything has to be shit, fall apart, result in disconnection and loss. All desires must remain unfulfilled). I suppose in some ways t</span>
  <span id="freeText16644415238793038775" style="display:none">This was a very interesting book, sensitively written and complex and managed to have elements of romance in it without putting me off too much (anyone who follows my reviews will be surprised by this). It's a tad on the bleak and tragic side, although at least it constantly humanises and rehumanises characters.<br /><br />Two of my gripes were the overall negativity of it (everything has to be shit, fall apart, result in disconnection and loss. All desires must remain unfulfilled). I suppose in some ways that is better than fluffy positivity, but not everyone will have the stamina to read it and at the end (after persisting so long) I was left feeling vaguely disappointed (less so than with for example "Burial rites" by Hannah Kent but still). I don't like it when the main message of a book seems to be that suffering and disappointment are inevitable and that there is nothing much else to the human condition.<br /><br />The other gripe was that even though there was a sprinkling of strong and relateable female characters, I don't actually think this book passes the Bechdel test. That is it was a book about men relating to men and women relating to men and there was no female relationship developed ANYWHERE in the book, each woman seemed to be an island surrounded only by men or unwilling to reach other to each other. I don't accept this as believable AND I don't enjoy reading it. I'm not saying every book needs to throw in a lesbian romance (though I would enjoy reading that) but something...a friendship, a mother daughter relationship, sisters that actually get along, allies, ANYTHING!<br /><br />I didn't like the constant shifting between first and third person, I have heard it suggested that only having first person from one character can be considered "boring" by some readers. I find it interferes with my "suspended disbelief" to have the shifts in POV this radical and abrupt and I thought that was a weakness in otherwise very strong writing. Perhaps then, there were also too many "main" characters.<br /><br />Ok so I have said what I didn't like. What I did like was the humanity of the diverse characters (male, female, white, "Indian", shifting ethnic boundaries (and other types of boundaries), mad, gay, sexually transgressive etc). The story gave us just enough information without making everything too clear (and it unfolded masterfully). I've critiqued the negativity but I suppose there were traces of hope and meaning within it. Love is a complex thing and connection is difficult. Loyalties shift, people don't fully know themselves. The character of Susannah was a stereotype but I would have wanted to see more of Maria. She is left on the outskirts of the story to some degree.<br /><br />In any case I would recommend this book as a lot better than average. I will read more from Stef Penney (with the fantastic first name) especially if it is more recently written than this. I hope she does more with female characters in future works. Mrs Ross is a damn good start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16644415238793038775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_871735666" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/871735666" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1367916-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217203800p2/1367916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/871735666?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/1367916-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer871735666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15573191799002983361">My sister recommended this during a Sunday afternoon phone chat. My husband found it for me at Sequoya Library just before they closed for the day. Finished it Monday night. Impossible to go slow — esp. being sick and doing nothing but reading. Penney is a screenwriter and lives in Edinburgh, the locale where many of the people in this story lived before they went to Canada where the story is set.<br/><br/>Late in the 1860s in a small town in Canada, a semi-disabled trapper is murdered. A local woman find</span>
  <span id="freeText15573191799002983361" style="display:none">My sister recommended this during a Sunday afternoon phone chat. My husband found it for me at Sequoya Library just before they closed for the day. Finished it Monday night. Impossible to go slow — esp. being sick and doing nothing but reading. Penney is a screenwriter and lives in Edinburgh, the locale where many of the people in this story lived before they went to Canada where the story is set.<br /><br />Late in the 1860s in a small town in Canada, a semi-disabled trapper is murdered. A local woman finds the body and alerts the town magistrate who sends for representatives of the Hudson’s Bay Company, the man’s former employer, to investigate. Not long after, the woman realizes her 17-year-old son — a friend of the dead man — has disappeared, making him the prime suspect. Until an Indian acquaintance of the dead man is discovered at the murder site. <br /><br />Thus is set in motion an adventure that might have come from Jack London with its evocation of the struggle to survive out in the wilderness in winter. Who committed the murder and why is only one thread in Penney’s tale of tangled lives. Dozens of characters weave in and out of the chapters, revealing new facets of themselves and deepening the mystery. Every character is a fully-drawn, nuanced portrait. It’s noteworthy in a book with a number of female characters — white and Indian — that Penney never plays down their strengths, yet they don’t feel like modern feminists thrown into a 19th C. setting.<br /><br />The young man goes in search of his friend’s murderer. His mother and the Indian suspect take off after the boy. The Company men follow them. I must say there is nothing more perfect than reading about people searching, tracking, camping, getting lost, and bobbing and weaving in the winter in Canada as we wait for our own cold, endless winter to end. Unbelievable as it seems, Penney apparently has never been to Canada but I found her descriptions of the landscape and the weather formidable. Penney also had the right tone for every scene: She ranged from a dry, self-deprecating humor that one of the characters uses to describe her life in an insane asylum in Edinburgh, to an eloquent appraisal of the lives of the Indians after white men arrive and begin the big business of fur trading.<br /><br />A wonderful book that I hated to finish, especially since it appears Penney has only written one other.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15573191799002983361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112198865" />
    <a title="Merty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2155468-merty"><img alt="Merty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238102670p2/2155468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112198865?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merty" href="/user/show/2155468-merty">Merty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112198865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5754724305081063811">I LOVED this book, one of the best books I've read this year. If only more books were written like this!!! This was the best book to read while there is a heatwave outside, as this story tells the tale of an isolated settlement at Dove River during a snowy wasteland with wolves. This book was a thriller/mystery and historical romance set in a less populated backwood of Canada. Told from different points of view that kept me reading late into the night. Since there where a constant change of poin</span>
  <span id="freeText5754724305081063811" style="display:none">I LOVED this book, one of the best books I've read this year. If only more books were written like this!!! This was the best book to read while there is a heatwave outside, as this story tells the tale of an isolated settlement at Dove River during a snowy wasteland with wolves. This book was a thriller/mystery and historical romance set in a less populated backwood of Canada. Told from different points of view that kept me reading late into the night. Since there where a constant change of points of view, it made me wonder where the author was taking me along the story. My only complaint about the book is that I felt it left things untied, made one wonder what happened to the characters, as what happened to them, but the author does mention this in an interview about ending a novel and that "endings are never neat, because when life goes on, there is no end." Interesting but not for the reader!!! It's going to be tough to read my next book now, as I really loved being inside the world of The Tenderness Of Wolves. I hope Stef Penney is writing another book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5754724305081063811" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/822703-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781847240675" href="/book/show/951457.The_Tenderness_of_Wolves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2567803281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12540001766959837349">I’m a little undecided on this rating, two or three. I’d prefer two and a half. It is well written the characters are developed and the environment well described.<br/><br/>There’s an awful lot of characters in the book, all with their own story. There’s also an great deal of mystery, either in the characters’ back story or in their current one. Their stories are all in the third person, except one, who is written in the first person. Not really sure why, doesn’t add anything.<br/><br/>With so many characters, at t</span>
  <span id="freeText12540001766959837349" style="display:none">I’m a little undecided on this rating, two or three. I’d prefer two and a half. It is well written the characters are developed and the environment well described.<br /><br />There’s an awful lot of characters in the book, all with their own story. There’s also an great deal of mystery, either in the characters’ back story or in their current one. Their stories are all in the third person, except one, who is written in the first person. Not really sure why, doesn’t add anything.<br /><br />With so many characters, at times I found I couldn’t recall them or what had happened to them a few chapters back. Each character their own complexities, all were built up, mostly for no reason. Too many of characters’ stories remained unexplained or felt unfinished. <br /><br />The whole book felt like a build up, to something that it didn’t get too. I’m not astounded to discover that the author is a screenwriter. Season one creates the characters and plot and leaves the viewer wanting, to ensure they’ll watch season two.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12540001766959837349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dNHfoc3ZlydpoU/o+swKxWbD8tRj9P8gLVjA18710306/sjUQCk4ZBwzqsoHuJTOWDk1PhChj6LZIbRWzUsbQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4+Lb7a0dKTD+vYF7af4fDIS7bDRWj9z++UGQVn03x0mtzcyYIO2Gc4svZFmUioEHukGr3iXarHwNOOTXfokPdw==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/181357.Stef_Penney">About Stef Penney</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/181357.Stef_Penney"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1236975318p3/181357.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/181357.Stef_Penney">Stef Penney
</a></div>

238
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15823729967157117423">Stef Penney grew up in the Scottish capital and turned to film-making after a degree in Philosophy and Theology from Bristol University. She made three short films before studying Film and TV at Bournemouth College of Art, and on graduation was selected for the Carlton Television New Writers Scheme. She has also written and directed two short films; a BBC 10 x 10 starring Anna Friel and a Film Cou</span>
  <span id="freeText15823729967157117423" style="display:none">Stef Penney grew up in the Scottish capital and turned to film-making after a degree in Philosophy and Theology from Bristol University. She made three short films before studying Film and TV at Bournemouth College of Art, and on graduation was selected for the Carlton Television New Writers Scheme. She has also written and directed two short films; a BBC 10 x 10 starring Anna Friel and a Film Council Digital Short in 2002 starring Lucy Russell.<br /><br />She won the 2006 Costa Book Awards with her debut novel The Tenderness of Wolves which is set in Canada in the 1860s. . As Stef Penney suffered from agoraphobia at the time of writing this novel, she did all the research in the libraries of London and never visited Canada.<br />-Wikipedia</span>
  <a data-text-id="15823729967157117423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
